## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of time and velocity. In nonlinear oscillator systems, the acceleration typically depends on position (which relates to velocity through integration) and velocity itself through restoring forces and damping terms. Since position is not directly given, the relationship may involve nonlinear functions of v and t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v (linear velocity-dependent damping/driving)
- Cubic nonlinearity (Duffing-type): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (nonlinear restoring force in velocity space)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v (nonlinear damping with amplitude-dependent sign change)
- Polynomial restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 (general polynomial nonlinearity in velocity)
- Sinusoidal driving with damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (damped oscillator with periodic forcing)
- Harmonic restoring via trig: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v (position approximated as sinusoidal function of time)
- Combined trig and nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (forced Duffing-like oscillator)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * v * abs(v) + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (velocity-squared damping with forcing)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping with driving)
- Cosine restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (multi-frequency restoring force)
- Position as integral proxy: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (acceleration as derivative of sinusoidal velocity)
- Nonlinear pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * v) (pendulum-type restoring force in velocity representation)
- Mixed polynomial-trig: dv_dt = c0 * v**2 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v (parametric-like coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Nonlinear restoring force → odd-power polynomials in displacement/velocity (v, v**3, v**5) preserving symmetry
- Self-sustained oscillation → terms like (1 - v**2)*v indicating amplitude-dependent energy balance (Van der Pol type)
- Hidden position dependence → sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) as proxy for position when only t and v are available
- Phase space structure → acceleration depending on both v and implicit position suggests combined trig(t) and polynomial(v) terms
- Frequency mixing in nonlinear systems → products of trig functions or multiple frequency components sin(c1*t) + sin(c2*t)
- Energy-based constraints → acceleration terms that can be written as gradients of potential energy, e.g., dv_dt = -dU/dx expressed through v
- Amplitude-dependent frequency → coupling between v**2 and trig(t) terms indicating frequency shifts with amplitude
- Conservative vs dissipative decomposition → separate even-in-v terms (dissipation) from odd-in-v terms (conservative forces)
